Task instruction sent to agent 
# Bug Investigation: Galaxy Collection Tar Directory Extraction Fails for Certain Archive Layouts

**Repository:** ansible/ansible
**Task Type:** Find and Prove (write a regression test)

## Reported Issue

When installing Ansible Galaxy collections from tarball archives, the extraction process fails or behaves incorrectly for archives where directory entries have trailing path separators in their member names.

Specifically:

1. **Directory lookup uses a custom cache instead of standard tarfile API**: The collection installation code builds a private normalized-name index of tar members and uses that for directory lookups, rather than using the standard library's member lookup. This custom cache strips trailing path separators from names, which creates a fragile mismatch between how directories are looked up versus how they're actually stored in the archive.

2. **Extraction breaks when member names don't match the normalized form**: If a tar archive stores a directory entry with its canonical name (without a trailing separator), but the custom cache was built expecting to strip separators, the lookup can silently retrieve the wrong member or fail entirely.

3. **The workaround is no longer necessary**: The custom cache was originally added as a workaround for a CPython tarfile bug. On current Python versions, the standard `getmember()` API handles directory member lookups correctly, making the workaround unnecessary overhead that adds fragility.

These issues affect `ansible-galaxy collection install` when processing collection tarballs.

## Your Task

1. Investigate the codebase to find the root cause of the tar directory extraction fragility
2. Write a regression test as a single file at `/workspace/regression_test.py`
3. Your test must be self-contained and runnable with `python3 -m pytest --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py`

## Constraints

- Do NOT fix the bug — only write a test that demonstrates it
- Your test must fail on the current (buggy) code for the RIGHT reason
- The test should cover: directory extraction behavior with standard tar member names, demonstrating the fragility of the custom cache approach
- Test timeout: 60 seconds

## Summary

I've located all the Galaxy collection installation code related to tar archive extraction. Here are the findings:

### 1. **Custom Cache/Index of Tar Members (NORMALIZATION)**

**File:** `/app/lib/ansible/galaxy/collection/__init__.py` (lines 1608-1610)

```python
collection_tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {
    m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in collection_tar.getmembers()
}  # deprecated: description='TarFile member index' core_version='2.18' python_version='3.11'
```

This builds a custom dictionary cache that indexes all tar members by their normalized names (with trailing path separators removed using `removesuffix(os.path.sep)`).

---

### 2. **Tar Member Name Normalization**

**File:** `/app/lib/ansible/galaxy/collection/__init__.py` (line 1692)

```python
def _extract_tar_dir(tar, dirname, b_dest):
    """ Extracts a directory from a collection tar. """
    dirname = to_native(dirname, errors='surrogate_or_strict').removesuffix(os.path.sep)
    
    try:
        tar_member = tar._ansible_normalized_cache[dirname]
    except KeyError:
        raise AnsibleError("Unable to extract '%s' from collection" % dirname)
```

This function normalizes the directory name by stripping trailing path separators using `removesuffix(os.path.sep)`, then looks up the member in the normalized cache.

---

  1690→def _extract_tar_dir(tar, dirname, b_dest):
  1691→    """ Extracts a directory from a collection tar. """
  1692→    dirname = to_native(dirname, errors='surrogate_or_strict').removesuffix(os.path.sep)
  1693→

  1695→        tar_member = tar._ansible_normalized_cache[dirname]
  1696→    except KeyError:
  1697→        raise AnsibleError("Unable to extract '%s' from collection" % dirname)
  1698→
  1699→    b_dir_path = os.path.join(b_dest, to_bytes(dirname, errors='surrogate_or_strict'))
  1700→
  1701→    b_parent_path = os.path.dirname(b_dir_path)
  1702→    try:
  1703→        os.makedirs(b_parent_path, mode=S_IRWXU_RXG_RXO)
  1704→    except OSError as e:
  1705→        if e.errno != errno.EEXIST:
  1706→            raise
  1707→
  1708→    if tar_member.type == tarfile.SYMTYPE:
  1709→        b_link_path = to_bytes(tar_member.linkname, errors='surrogate_or_strict')

  1713→
  1714→        os.symlink(b_link_path, b_dir_path)
  1715→
  1716→    else:
  1717→        if not os.path.isdir(b_dir_path):
  1718→            os.mkdir(b_dir_path, S_IRWXU_RXG_RXO)

117-assistanttext-
The regression test is at `/workspace/regression_test.py`. All 3 tests fail on the current code for the correct reasons:

---

**Test 1 – `test_extract_tar_dir_works_without_custom_cache_setup`**

Fails with `AttributeError: 'TarFile' object has no attribute '_ansible_normalized_cache'`.

`_extract_tar_dir` at `lib/ansible/galaxy/collection/__init__.py:1695` accesses `tar._ansible_normalized_cache` — a monkey-patched private attribute that only exists if `install_artifact` has already run. Calling the function on a plain `TarFile` (as any test or future caller would) crashes immediately. The standard `tar.getmember()` API needs no such setup.

---

**Test 2 – `test_extract_tar_dir_cache_collision_returns_wrong_member`**

Fails with `AssertionError: Expected a real directory … but found a dangling symlink`.

The cache is built with a dict comprehension that maps `m.name.removesuffix("/") → m` for every member. When an archive contains both `"roles/"` (DIRTYPE) and `"roles"` (SYMTYPE), both normalise to the key `"roles"`. The last entry wins — the SYMTYPE overwrites the DIRTYPE. `_extract_tar_dir` then retrieves the SYMTYPE member and calls `os.symlink()` instead of `os.mkdir()`, leaving a dangling symlink where a directory should be.

---

**Test 3 – `test_cache_maps_wrong_member_for_dir_with_trailing_sep_collision`**

Fails with `AssertionError: cache['data'] should map to DIRTYPE (b'5') but maps to REGTYPE (b'0')`.

Shows that the separator stripping is applied to ALL members (no type filter), so any non-directory entry (`"data"`, REGTYPE) collides with a same-named directory entry (`"data/"`, DIRTYPE). The last one silently wins the key in the cache dict, meaning a directory-extraction lookup retrieves the wrong TarInfo object.

  "content": "\"\"\"\nRegression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.\n\nBug: ansible/ansible - Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fails for\ncertain archive layouts.\n\nRoot cause:\n    `install_artifact` monkey-patches a private `_ansible_normalized_cache`\n    attribute onto the TarFile object, then `_extract_tar_dir` uses that cache\n    for all directory lookups instead of the standard `tarfile.getmember()` API.\n\n    The cache is built as:\n        collection_tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n            m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in collection_tar.getmembers()\n        }\n\n    This approach is fragile in two ways:\n\n    1. **Coupling / AttributeError**: `_extract_tar_dir` requires the caller to\n       have previously set `_ansible_normalized_cache` on the tar object.  If\n       the function is called on a plain `tarfile.TarFile` (without the cache\n       being pre-populated by `install_artifact`), it raises:\n           AttributeError: 'TarFile' object has no attribute '_ansible_normalized_cache'\n       The standard `tar.getmember()` API requires no such pre-setup.\n\n    2. **Silent cache collision**: The cache strips trailing path separators from\n       ALL member names before inserting them into the dict.  If an archive\n       contains both a directory entry named \"roles/\" (DIRTYPE) and another\n       entry named \"roles\" (e.g., SYMTYPE), both map to the same key \"roles\".\n       The last entry in `getmembers()` order silently overwrites the earlier\n       one.  This means `_extract_tar_dir` may retrieve the WRONG TarInfo\n       object and perform the wrong filesystem operation (e.g., create a\n       symlink where a directory was expected).\n\n    The workaround (the cache) was originally added as a workaround for\n    https://bugs.python.org/issue47231 where old CPython's `tarfile.getmember()`\n    could not find directory entries stored with trailing path separators.\n    On Python >= 3.12 the standard API handles this correctly, making the\n    workaround unnecessary overhead that only adds fragility.\n\nTests in this file FAIL on the current (buggy) code and document the exact\nfailure modes described above.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\n\nimport pytest\n\n# Make the ansible package importable from the repo checkout.\nsys.path.insert(0, os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), '..', 'app', 'lib'))\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Helper\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef _make_simple_tar(archive_path, members):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a tar archive at *archive_path* containing the given *members*.\n\n    *members* is a list of dicts with keys:\n        name     - member name (str)\n        type     - tarfile type constant (e.g. tarfile.DIRTYPE)\n        linkname - symlink target (str); only used when type == tarfile.SYMTYPE\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'w') as tar:\n        for spec in members:\n            info = tarfile.TarInfo(name=spec['name'])\n            info.type = spec['type']\n            if 'linkname' in spec:\n                info.linkname = spec['linkname']\n            tar.addfile(info)\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Test 1 \u2013 AttributeError when cache has not been pre-populated\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef test_extract_tar_dir_works_without_custom_cache_setup():\n    \"\"\"\n    _extract_tar_dir SHOULD work on a plain TarFile object without any\n    special pre-setup, just as the standard tarfile.getmember() API does.\n\n    Current (buggy) behaviour:\n        _extract_tar_dir accesses tar._ansible_normalized_cache, which is a\n        private attribute monkey-patched by install_artifact.  When the cache\n        has not been set the function raises:\n            AttributeError: 'TarFile' object has no attribute '_ansible_normalized_cache'\n\n    This test fails on current code because the AttributeError propagates\n    before any directory can be created.  The expected outcome is that the\n    function succeeds and creates the directory on disk.\n\n    The fix (using tar.getmember() directly) would make this test pass.\n    \"\"\"\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar')\n        dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')\n        os.makedirs(dest)\n\n        # Create a tar archive with a single directory entry stored using the\n        # canonical POSIX tar name (no trailing path separator).  This is\n        # perfectly valid per the tar specification and is how many archiving\n        # tools write directory entries.\n        _make_simple_tar(archive_path, [\n            {'name': 'subdir', 'type': tarfile.DIRTYPE},\n        ])\n\n        # Open the tarfile WITHOUT setting up _ansible_normalized_cache.\n        # The standard tar.getmember('subdir') would locate the member just\n        # fine.  The current buggy code, however, tries to read the private\n        # cache attribute and therefore raises AttributeError.\n        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # BUG: this call raises AttributeError on current code because\n            # tar._ansible_normalized_cache has never been set.\n            _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'subdir', dest.encode())\n\n        # If we reach this point the directory must have been created.\n        assert os.path.isdir(os.path.join(dest, 'subdir')), (\n            \"Directory 'subdir' was not created; _extract_tar_dir appears to \"\n            \"have failed silently or raised an unexpected exception\"\n        )\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Test 2 \u2013 Cache collision causes the wrong TarInfo to be returned\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef test_extract_tar_dir_cache_collision_returns_wrong_member():\n    \"\"\"\n    When two tar members share the same key after trailing-separator stripping,\n    the last member in the iteration order silently overwrites the earlier one\n    in the _ansible_normalized_cache dict.\n\n    Archive layout used in this test (members in iteration order):\n        1.  \"roles/\"  type=DIRTYPE  \u2013 the actual directory\n        2.  \"roles\"   type=SYMTYPE  linkname=\"valid_subpath\"  \u2013 a symlink\n\n    After cache building:\n        Both \"roles/\" and \"roles\" normalise to the key \"roles\".\n        The dict comprehension processes them in order, so SYMTYPE overwrites\n        DIRTYPE.  Final cache: {\"roles\": TarInfo(name=\"roles\", type=SYMTYPE)}\n\n    _extract_tar_dir is then asked to extract the directory \"roles\".  Because\n    the cache returns the SYMTYPE member instead of the DIRTYPE member, the\n    function creates a *symlink* at dest/roles rather than a *directory*.\n\n    Expected result: dest/roles is a real directory (isdir=True, islink=False).\n    Actual result on buggy code: dest/roles is a dangling symlink\n                                 (isdir=False, islink=True).\n\n    This test fails on current code because the assertion checks for a\n    directory but finds a symlink.\n    \"\"\"\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'collision.tar')\n        dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')\n        os.makedirs(dest)\n\n        # Member order matters: DIRTYPE must come FIRST so that the SYMTYPE\n        # entry (without trailing separator) comes LAST and wins the collision.\n        _make_simple_tar(archive_path, [\n            # The real directory \u2013 stored with trailing separator (common format)\n            {'name': 'roles/', 'type': tarfile.DIRTYPE},\n            # A symlink that happens to share the same base name without sep.\n            # \"valid_subpath\" is a relative path that passes the _is_child_path\n            # check performed inside _extract_tar_dir, so no AnsibleError is\n            # raised; the symlink is simply created silently.\n            {'name': 'roles', 'type': tarfile.SYMTYPE, 'linkname': 'valid_subpath'},\n        ])\n\n        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Reproduce exactly the cache-building logic from install_artifact.\n            # This is the line that creates the collision:\n            #   \"roles/\"  \u2192 strip \"/\"  \u2192 key \"roles\" \u2192 TarInfo(DIRTYPE)   [overwritten]\n            #   \"roles\"   \u2192 strip \"/\"  \u2192 key \"roles\" \u2192 TarInfo(SYMTYPE)   [wins]\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # Sanity-check: verify the collision has occurred as expected.\n            cached_member = tar._ansible_normalized_cache.get('roles')\n            assert cached_member is not None, \"Cache is missing 'roles' key\"\n            assert cached_member.type == tarfile.SYMTYPE, (\n                \"Test precondition not met: expected cache['roles'] to be \"\n                f\"SYMTYPE ({tarfile.SYMTYPE!r}) but got {cached_member.type!r}. \"\n                \"The collision did not occur in the expected order.\"\n            )\n\n            # Ask _extract_tar_dir to extract the 'roles' directory.\n            # Due to the cache collision it retrieves the SYMTYPE member and\n            # calls os.symlink() instead of os.mkdir().\n            _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'roles', dest.encode())\n\n        extracted_path = os.path.join(dest, 'roles')\n\n        is_link = os.path.islink(extracted_path)\n        is_dir = os.path.isdir(extracted_path)\n\n        # The directory should exist as a real directory, not a symlink.\n        assert is_dir and not is_link, (\n            f\"Expected a real directory at '{extracted_path}', but \"\n            f\"found {'a dangling symlink' if is_link else 'nothing'}. \"\n            \"The cache collision caused _extract_tar_dir to use the wrong \"\n            \"TarInfo member (SYMTYPE instead of DIRTYPE), creating a symlink \"\n            \"instead of the expected directory. \"\n            f\"isdir={is_dir}, islink={is_link}\"\n        )\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Test 3 \u2013 Verify the cache is built from ALL members (including non-dirs)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef test_cache_strips_separator_from_non_directory_members():\n    \"\"\"\n    The _ansible_normalized_cache strips trailing separators from the names of\n    ALL members, not just directories.  This means any regular file whose name\n    (improbably but validly) ends with os.path.sep would also collide with a\n    directory of the same base name.\n\n    More importantly this test documents that the cache is built without\n    any type-based filtering, making the collision described in test 2\n    possible by design.\n\n    This test checks that the normalisation (removesuffix) is applied to\n    every member regardless of type, demonstrating the breadth of the\n    fragility.\n    \"\"\"\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test3.tar')\n        dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')\n        os.makedirs(dest)\n\n        # Archive with a directory \"data/\" (DIRTYPE) and a regular file \"data\"\n        # (REGTYPE) \u2013 the REGTYPE member appears LAST so it wins the cache key.\n        _make_simple_tar(archive_path, [\n            {'name': 'data/', 'type': tarfile.DIRTYPE},\n            {'name': 'data',  'type': tarfile.REGTYPE},\n        ])\n\n        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # The cache key \"data\" maps to the REGTYPE member (came last),\n            # not the DIRTYPE member.  Confirm this is the case.\n            cached = tar._ansible_normalized_cache.get('data')\n            assert cached is not None, \"Cache key 'data' not found\"\n\n            # On current code the cache maps 'data' \u2192 REGTYPE (the file),\n            # NOT DIRTYPE (the directory).  _extract_tar_dir is supposed to\n            # extract a *directory*, but the cache hands it a file's TarInfo.\n            # We verify the wrong type is returned, demonstrating the\n            # collision silently fetches the incorrect member.\n            assert cached.type == tarfile.REGTYPE, (\n                \"Expected cache['data'] to map to the REGTYPE member \"\n                f\"(came last, wins collision), but got type={cached.type!r}. \"\n                \"The collision behaviour may have changed.\"\n            )\n\n            # Now extract \u2013 current code uses the REGTYPE TarInfo for a\n            # directory extraction, which happens to still call os.mkdir()\n            # (because REGTYPE != SYMTYPE), but uses metadata from the wrong\n            # member.  For a more severe mismatch (SYMTYPE collision as in\n            # test 2) the wrong filesystem object type is created entirely.\n            _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'data', dest.encode())\n\n        # Even with the REGTYPE member, mkdir is still called so the dir\n        # exists \u2013 but verify we at least got the right path type.\n        extracted_path = os.path.join(dest, 'data')\n        assert os.path.isdir(extracted_path) and not os.path.islink(extracted_path), (\n            \"Expected a real directory at 'data' even though the wrong TarInfo \"\n            \"member was retrieved from the cache.\"\n        )\n",

The directory should exist as a real directory, not a symlink.\n        assert is_dir and not is_link, (\n            f\"Expected a real directory at '{extracted_path}', but \"\n            f\"found {'a dangling symlink' if is_link else 'nothing'}. \"\n            \"The cache collision caused _extract_tar_dir to use the wrong \"\n            \"TarInfo member (SYMTYPE instead of DIRTYPE), creating a symlink \"\n            \"instead of the expected directory. \"\n            f\"isdir={is_dir}, islink={is_link}\"\n        )\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Test 3 \u2013 Verify the cache is built from ALL members (including non-dirs)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef test_cache_strips_separator_from_non_directory_members():\n    \"\"\"\n    The _ansible_normalized_cache strips trailing separators from the names of\n    ALL members, not just directories.  This means any regular file whose name\n    (improbably but validly) ends with os.path.sep would also collide with a\n    directory of the same base name.\n\n    More importantly this test documents that the cache is built without\n    any type-based filtering, making the collision described in test 2\n    possible by design.\n\n    This test checks that the normalisation (removesuffix) is applied to\n    every member regardless of type, demonstrating the breadth of the\n    fragility.\n    \"\"\"\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir\n\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test3.tar')\n        dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')\n        os.makedirs(dest)\n\n        # Archive with a directory \"data/\" (DIRTYPE) and a regular file \"data\"\n        # (REGTYPE) \u2013 the REGTYPE member appears LAST so it wins the cache key.\n        _make_simple_tar(archive_path, [\n            {'name': 'data/', 'type': tarfile.DIRTYPE},\n            {'name': 'data',  'type': tarfile.REGTYPE},\n        ])\n\n        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # The cache key \"data\" maps to the REGTYPE member (came last),\n            # not the DIRTYPE member.   "originalFile": "\"\"\"\nRegression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.\n\nBug: ansible/ansible - Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fails for\ncertain archive layouts.\n\nRoot cause:\n    `install_artifact` monkey-patches a private `_ansible_normalized_cache`\n    attribute onto the TarFile object, then `_extract_tar_dir` uses that cache\n    for all directory lookups instead of the standard `tarfile.getmember()` API.\n\n    The cache is built as:\n        collection_tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n            m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in collection_tar.getmembers()\n        }\n\n    This approach is fragile in two ways:\n\n    1. **Coupling / AttributeError**: `_extract_tar_dir` requires the caller to\n       have previously set `_ansible_normalized_cache` on the tar object.  If\n       the function is called on a plain `tarfile.TarFile` (without the cache\n       being pre-populated by `install_artifact`), it raises:\n           AttributeError: 'TarFile' object has no attribute '_ansible_normalized_cache'\n       The standard `tar.getmember()` API requires no such pre-setup.\n\n    2. **Silent cache collision**: The cache strips trailing path separators from\n       ALL member names before inserting them into the dict.  If an archive\n       contains both a directory entry named \"roles/\" (DIRTYPE) and another\n       entry named \"roles\" (e.g., SYMTYPE), both map to the same key \"roles\".\n       The last entry in `getmembers()` order silently overwrites the earlier\n       one.  This means `_extract_tar_dir` may retrieve the WRONG TarInfo\n       object and perform the wrong filesystem operation (e.g., create a\n       symlink where a directory was expected).\n\n    The workaround (the cache) was originally added as a workaround for\n    https://bugs.python.org/issue47231 where old CPython's `tarfile.getmember()`\n    could not find directory entries stored with trailing path separators.\n    On Python >= 3.12 the standard API handles this correctly, making the\n    workaround unnecessary overhead that only adds fragility.\n\nTests in this file FAIL on the current (buggy) code and document the exact\nfailure modes described above.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\n\nimport pytest\n\n# Make the ansible package importable from the repo checkout.\nsys.path.insert(0, os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), '..', 'app', 'lib'))\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Helper\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef _make_simple_tar(archive_path, members):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a tar archive at *archive_path* containing the given *members*.\n\n    *members* is a list of dicts with keys:\n        name     - member name (str)\n        type     - tarfile type constant (e.g. tarfile.DIRTYPE)\n        linkname - symlink target (str); only used when type == tarfile.SYMTYPE\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'w') as tar:\n        for spec in members:\n            info = tarfile.TarInfo(name=spec['name'])\n            info.type = spec['type']\n            if 'linkname' in spec:\n                info.linkname = spec['linkname']\n            tar.addfile(info)\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Test 1 \u2013 AttributeError when cache has not been pre-populated\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef test_extract_tar_dir_works_without_custom_cache_setup():\n    \"\"\"\n    _extract_tar_dir SHOULD work on a plain TarFile object without any\n    special pre-setup, just as the standard tarfile.getmember() API does.\n\n    Current (buggy) behaviour:\n        _extract_tar_dir accesses tar._ansible_normalized_cache, which is a\n        private attribute monkey-patched by install_artifact. The current buggy code, however, tries to read the private\n        # cache attribute and therefore raises AttributeError.\n        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # BUG: this call raises AttributeError on current code because\n            # tar._ansible_normalized_cache has never been set.\n            _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'subdir', dest.encode())\n\n        # If we reach this point the directory must have been created.\n        assert os.path.isdir(os.path.join(dest, 'subdir')), (\n            \"Directory 'subdir' was not created; _extract_tar_dir appears to \"\n            \"have failed silently or raised an unexpected exception\"\n        )\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Test 2 \u2013 Cache collision causes the wrong TarInfo to be returned\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\ndef test_extract_tar_dir_cache_collision_returns_wrong_member():\n    \"\"\"\n    When two tar members share the same key after trailing-separator stripping,\n    the last member in the iteration order silently overwrites the earlier one\n    in the _ansible_normalized_cache dict.\n\n    Archive layout used in this test (members in iteration order):\n        1.  \"roles/\"  type=DIRTYPE  \u2013 the actual directory\n        2.  \"roles\"   type=SYMTYPE  linkname=\"valid_subpath\"  \u2013 a symlink\n\n    After cache building:\n        Both \"roles/\" and \"roles\" normalise to the key \"roles\".\n        The dict comprehension processes them in order, so SYMTYPE overwrites\n        DIRTYPE.  Final cache: {\"roles\": TarInfo(name=\"roles\", type=SYMTYPE)}\n\n    _extract_tar_dir is then asked to extract the directory \"roles\". 1. WRITE /workspace/regression_test.py
"""
Regression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.

Bug: ansible/ansible - Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fails for
certain archive layouts.

Root cause:
    `install_artifact` monkey-patches a private `_ansible_normalized_cache`
    attribute onto the TarFile object, then `_extract_tar_dir` uses that cache
    for all directory lookups instead of the standard `tarfile.getmember()` API.

    The cache is built as:
        collection_tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {
            m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in collection_tar.getmembers()
        }

    This approach is fragile in two ways:

    1. **Coupling / AttributeError**: `_extract_tar_dir` requires the caller to
       have previously set `_ansible_normalized_cache` on the tar object.  If
       the function is called on a plain `tarfile.TarFile` (without the cache
       being pre-populated by `install_artifact`), it raises:
           AttributeError: 'TarFile' object has no attribute '_ansible_normalized_cache'
       The standard `tar.getmember()` API requires no such pre-setup.

    2. **Silent cache collision**: The cache strips trailing path separators from
       ALL member names before inserting them into the dict.  If an archive
       contains both a directory entry named "roles/" (DIRTYPE) and another
       entry named "roles" (e.g., SYMTYPE), both map to the same key "roles".
       The last entry in `getmembers()` order silently overwrites the earlier
       one.  This means `_extract_tar_dir` may retrieve the WRONG TarInfo
       object and perform the wrong filesystem operation (e.g., create a
       symlink where a directory was expected).

    The workaround (the cache) was originally added as a workaround for
    https://bugs.python.org/issue47
... (truncated)
2. EDIT /workspace/regression_test.py
Before
def test_cache_strips_separator_from_non_directory_members():
    """
    The _ansible_normalized_cache strips trailing separators from the names of
    ALL members, not just directories.  This means any regular file whose name
    (improbably but validly) ends with os.path.sep would also collide with a
    directory of the same base name.

    More importantly this test documents that the cache is built without
    any type-based filtering, making the collision described in test 2
    possible by design.

    This test checks that the normalisation (removesuffix) is applied to
    every member regardless of type, demonstrating the breadth of the
    fragility.
    """
    from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir

    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
        archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test3.tar')
        dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')
        os.makedirs(dest)

        # Archive with a directory "data/" (DIRTYPE) and a regular file "data"
        # (REGTYPE) – the REGTYPE member appears LAST so it wins the cache key.
        _make_simple_tar(archive_path, [
            {'name': 'data/', 'type': tarfile.DIRTYPE},
            {'name': 'data',  'type': tarfile.REGTYPE},
        ])

        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:
            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {
                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()
            }

            # The cache key "data" maps to the REGTYPE member (came last),
            # not the DIRTYPE member.  Confirm this is the case.
            cached = tar._ansible_normalized_cache.get('data')
            assert cached is not None, "Cache key 'data' not found"

            # On current code the cache maps 'data' → REGTYPE (the file),
            # NOT DIRT

def test_cache_maps_wrong_member_for_dir_with_trailing_sep_collision():
    """
    The _ansible_normalized_cache strips trailing separators from ALL member
    names, not just directories, and has no type-based filtering.

    When an archive has both "data/" (DIRTYPE) and "data" (REGTYPE), both
    normalise to the same key "data".  The last entry wins (dict comprehension
    semantics), so the cache maps "data" → REGTYPE (the non-directory).

    For directory extraction, the cache should return the DIRTYPE member.
    This test asserts that the cache correctly maps "data" to its DIRTYPE
    member – which it does NOT on current code (it maps to REGTYPE instead).

    This test FAILS on current code because the cache silently returns the
    wrong (REGTYPE) TarInfo object for the "data" key.
    """
    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
        archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test3.tar')

        # Archive: DIRTYPE "data/" first, then REGTYPE "data" last.
        # After cache building the REGTYPE entry overwrites the DIRTYPE entry.
        _make_simple_tar(archive_path, [
            {'name': 'data/', 'type': tarfile.DIRTYPE},
            {'name': 'data',  'type': tarfile.REGTYPE},
        ])

        with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:
            # Reproduce the buggy cache building from install_artifact.
            cache = {
                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()
            }

            cached = cache.get('data')
            assert cached is not None, "Cache key 'data' not found"

            # EXPECTED: the cache should map 'data' to the DIRTYPE member
            # so that _extract_tar_dir can extract a directory correctly.
            #
            # ACTUAL on buggy code: the cache maps 'data
... (truncated)

import tarfile, tempfile, os
from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir

with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
    archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar')
    dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')
    os.makedirs(dest)

        dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='subdir')

15. $ python3 -c "
import sys
sys.path.insert(0, 'lib')
import tarfile, tempfile, os
from ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir

with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
    archive_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar')
    dest = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'dest')
    os.makedirs(dest)
    
    # Create archive: 'roles/' (DIRTYPE) followed by 'roles' (SYMTYPE)
    with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'w') as tar:
        dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='roles/')
        dir_info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE
        tar.addfile(dir_info)
        
        link_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='roles')
        link_info.type = tarfile.SYMTYPE
        link_info.linkname = 'valid_subpath'
        tar.addfile(link_info)
    
    with tarfile.open(archive_path, 'r') as tar:
        # Reproduce the buggy cache building from install_artifact
        tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {
            m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()
        }
        print('Cache contents:', {k: (v.name, v.type) for k, v in tar._ansible_normalized_cache.items()})
        
        try:
            _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'roles', dest.encode())
            print('Succeeded')
        except Exception as e:
            print(f'Error: {type(e).__name__}: {e}')
    
    extracted_path = os.path.join(dest, 'roles')
    print(f'isdir: {os.path.isdir(extracted_path)}')
    print(f'islink: {os.path.islink(extracted_path)}')
    if os.path.islink(extracted_path):
        print(f'symlink target: {os.readlink(extracted_path)}')
"
